CSI SAP2000 22.0.0 installation file only ğŸ‘‡ğŸ‘‡
09:44
In reply to this message
New Features:

Multiple copies of the same model can now be run on different machines, and the analysis results merged together on a single machine for performing design and processing results. This can be particularly useful for running a large number of load cases (e.g., earthquakes for performance-based design, P-delta load cases for design by the Direct Analysis Method, etc.), and there are multiple machines available for running different load cases simultaneously.

An enhancement has been implemented in the concrete frame design codes ACI 318-14, ACI 318-11, and ACI 318-08 in which the delta_ns factor is now limited to 1.4 based on sections 6.2.6 and 6.6.4.5.1 of ACI 318-14, section 10.10.2.1 of ACI 318-11, and section 10.10.2.1 of ACI 318-08.

An enhancement has been made to the steel frame design codes Eurocode 3-2005, Italian NTC2008, and Italian NTC2018 in which the expression of Mcr is now being calculated according to Equation F.2 in Section F.1.2 of EC3:1993. It includes the C2*zg and C3*zj terms, where zg is the distance between the load application point and the shear center (zs), zj is defined in EC3:1993 Section F.1.2, and C2 and C3 are coefficients which depend on load conditions. Previously these terms were ignored and a simplified version of the formula for Mcr was being used. The term C2*zg considers the destabilizing effect of a compressive load placed on top of the beam and that passes through the shear center. This term can be ignored when either the bending moment diagram is linear along a part of a member due to restraints or when the load is applied at the shear center and therefore no destabilizing moments can occur. However, the term C2*zg cannot be assumed as zero for simply supported beams without lateral restraint and with the load applied at the top or bottom flanges. The second term C3*zj considers the effect of the section being singly-symmetric. The results were previously unconservative when the load was destabilizing and the beam was a deep beam.

An enhancement has been made to improve reporting for all concrete frame design codes for columns in which the reported design axial forces and bending moments were reported apparently randomly instead of the maximum values of a multi-valued combination, especially when the required rebar was the minimum. This also happened when a combination for which the case of minimum eccentricity moment about one of the axes was to be reported. Now the program reports the worst set of forces even if the rebar is not affected. This was not a bug. No design results are affected.

Obayashi Hybrid Brake Damper Stud Type damper
01:21
In reply to this message
The newly developed â€œHybrid Brake Damper Stud Typeâ€ combines a brake damper (* 1) and a viscoelastic damper (* 2) in series, so that both dampers complement each other and greatly reduce various shaking. You. The viscoelastic body is deformed to reduce the shaking in the case of minute shaking such as wind shaking or shaking in small and medium-sized earthquakes. In the case of large earthquakes, a brake damper is added to absorb the shaking. In this way, the combination of two vibration suppression functions in one unit increases the degree of freedom in architectural planning and reduces the cost of installing a vibration suppression system by up to 40%. Also, since maintenance and inspections are not required, the life cycle cost of the building can be reduced.

Obayashi has commercialized a hybrid brake damper brace type vibration control device mainly for steel structures, and the newly developed hybrid brake damper stud type has been applied to any building regardless of its structural form. Application is now possible. We will continue to proactively propose the adoption of a "hybrid brake damper" that has excellent damping performance, is maintenance-free, and has a high cost performance, by improving the damping performance of the building, thereby improving the living environment and extending the life of the building. I want to contribute to society.

* 1: Brake damper: A type of friction damper that applies the mechanism of automobile braking and absorbs shaking during a large earthquake by friction between the rake material and stainless steel plate.

* 2: Visco-elastic damper: Absorbs the energy of the sway of a wind or small / medium earthquake due to the resistance of a visco-elastic body that combines the properties of a spring and a viscous body.
01:22
Obayashi Hybrid Brake Damper Stud Type damper
01:25
Obayashi hybrid brake damper (friction+viscoelastic) 2006
01:25
In reply to this message
In collaboration with Professor Kazuhiko Kasai of Tokyo Institute of Technology, Obayashi has developed a " hybrid brake damper " that combines a viscoelastic damper with a vibration damping device (*) already developed and put into practical use by Obayashi.
By combining two dampers with different characteristics, it is possible to greatly reduce various types of shaking, from small shaking such as wind shaking to large shaking during a large earthquake.

* Brake damper: A friction damper developed by Obayashi Corporation that uses the mechanism of automobile braking and absorbs the shaking of earthquakes by friction between the brake material and stainless steel plate. It has already been applied to many buildings.

In recent years, many buildings, such as skyscrapers, whose height is extremely high compared to their width (the tower ratio is large) have been constructed. Buildings with a large tower ratio are greatly affected by shaking such as typhoons and earthquakes, and are required to have vibration damping performance that can respond to various shaking.
At present, methods for securing the vibration-damping performance of buildings with a large tower-to-ratio ratio include a method that uses a viscous damping wall and a device that reduces earthquake sway and a device that reduces wind sway separately. The method is adopted. However, these methods have had problems in terms of building construction constraints and costs.

The hybrid brake damper developed this time combines a brake damper that reduces the sway of an earthquake and a viscoelastic damper that reduces small sway such as wind sway. It is a vibration device.
By incorporating it as a brace in a structural frame composed of columns and beams, it is possible to handle from wind sway to earthquake sway. The viscoelastic body is deformed to reduce shaking in the case of minute shaking such as wind shaking or shaking in small and medium-sized earthquakes. Absorb.
Since the number of vibration suppression devices that have been separately installed for wind and earthquake countermeasures can be reduced, the degree of freedom in building planning is increased and the cost of introducing a vibration suppression system is 40%. Can be reduced to a degree.

The features of the hybrid brake damper are as follows.

Can handle small to large swings

By combining a brake damper that reduces the sway of an earthquake and a visco-elastic damper that reduces small sway such as wind sway, it can respond to various sways. By introducing this damper, small shaking such as wind shaking and large shaking during an earthquake can be reduced to about 2/3 each.

An economical damping device

Previously, buildings with large tower-to-tower ratios were equipped with a separate device to reduce wind sway and a damper for earthquakes, or used viscous damping walls, but hybrid brake dampers can cope with both sways. In addition, the number of vibration suppression devices can be reduced, and the cost of the vibration suppression devices can be reduced to about 2/3.

Greater freedom of design

Since the number of vibration dampers previously installed separately for wind sway and earthquake can be reduced, the degree of freedom in architectural planning is increased.
There are two types of hybrid brake dampers with different shapes, and these can be used separately.
Type 1 (Fig. 1) is a type in which a viscoelastic damper and a brake damper are arranged in series. The device is easier to manufacture than type 2, and has the advantage of being more economical.
Type 2 (Fig. 2) is a type in which a viscoelastic body is distributed around a steel pipe with a built-in brake damper. Its 230mm width allows it to be installed in narrow places.

In reply to this message
The hybrid brake damper was tested at the Obayashi Technical Research Institute and at the Kasai Laboratory at Tokyo Tech to confirm its performance. In addition, the validity of the manufacturing method and design method is confirmed by testing full-scale models. Obayashi will actively propose this hybrid brake damper to high-rise office buildings, apartment buildings, and pencil buildings.

Obayashi "Laputa 2D" Super-Active Vibration Control Technology
01:37
In reply to this message
Obayashi has developed "Laputa 2D," the world's first super-active vibration control technology that can buffer seismic forces to reduce building tremors to one-fiftieth the magnitude of ground tremors. A rubber base and actuator are installed beneath the building.

Ú©Ø§Ù†Ø§Ù„ Ø¬Ø¯Ø§Ø³Ø§Ø²ÛŒ Ù„Ø±Ø²Ù‡ Ø§ÛŒØŒ Ø³ÛŒØ³ØªÙ… Ù‡Ø§ÛŒ Ù…ÛŒØ±Ø§ÛŒÛŒ (Ù…ÛŒØ±Ø§Ú¯Ø±) Ø§Ù†Ø±Ú˜ÛŒ Ùˆ Ú©Ù†ØªØ±Ù„ Ø§Ø±ØªØ¹Ø§Ø´Ø§Øª
Fazlur Rahman Khan (Bengali: à¦«à¦œà¦²à§à¦° à¦°à¦¹à¦®à¦¾à¦¨ à¦–à¦¾à¦¨, Fozlur RÃ´hman Khan) (3 April 1929 â€“ 27 March 1982) was a Bangladeshi-American[2] structural engineer and architect, who initiated important structural systems for skyscrapers.[3][4][5] Considered the "father of tubular designs" for high-rises,[6] Khan was also a pioneer in computer-aided design (CAD). He was the structural engineer of the Sears Tower working with Architect Bruce Graham, since renamed Willis Tower, the tallest building in the world from 1973 until 1998, and the 100-story John Hancock Center.

Khan, more than any other individual, ushered in a renaissance in skyscraper construction during the second half of the 20th century.[7][8] He has been called the "Einstein of structural engineering" and the "Greatest Structural Engineer of the 20th Century" for his innovative use of structural systems that remain fundamental to modern skyscraper design and construction.[3][9] In his honor, the Council on Tall Buildings and Urban Habitat established the Fazlur Khan Lifetime Achievement Medal, as one of their CTBUH Skyscraper Awards.

Although best known for skyscrapers, Khan was also an active designer of other kinds of structures, including the Hajj airport terminal, the McMathâ€“Pierce solar telescope, and several stadium structures.
